## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x and time t. The acceleration represents the net force per unit mass, combining nonlinear restoring forces in x and possibly explicit time-dependent driving forces.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear restoring force: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple harmonic oscillator)
- Cubic nonlinearity (Duffing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (Duffing oscillator without driving)
- Driven Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (Duffing oscillator with periodic driving)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic potential)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric potential)
- Mixed polynomial: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (general anharmonic oscillator)
- Driven linear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (driven harmonic oscillator)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (parametrically driven oscillator)
- Softening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2)**(-1) (rational restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (pendulum / sinusoidal restoring force)
- Driven cubic: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (general driven Duffing)
- Inverse cubic force: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**(-3) (modified oscillator with singular potential)
- Piecewise-linear approximation: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * abs(x) (piecewise quadratic potential)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-symmetry restoring force → Only odd powers of x (x, x**3, x**5) indicating symmetric potential well
- Hardening vs softening spring → Positive coefficient on x**3 (with negative linear term) indicates hardening; negative indicates softening
- Periodic driving force → Additive sinusoidal or cosine terms in t, independent of x
- Parametric excitation → Multiplicative coupling between x and periodic function of t (e.g., x*cos(c*t))
- Conservative system without velocity dependence → Acceleration depends only on x (gradient of potential), no explicit t dependence
- Sinusoidal restoring force → sin(c*x) indicates periodic potential (e.g., pendulum), approximated by polynomial for small x
- Bounded potential escape → Negative highest-order polynomial term allows unbounded trajectories beyond separatrix
- Multi-frequency driving → Sum of sinusoids with different frequencies in t indicates quasi-periodic forcing
- Amplitude-dependent frequency → Nonlinear x terms cause frequency to shift with oscillation amplitude (backbone curve behavior)

2. A term `x*exp(-|x|)`: `-1.15357*x*exp(-|x|)`
3. A `sin(t)` term: `0.42262*sin(t)`

Note that `sin(t) = cos(t - π/2)`, so `cos(c + t)` terms can represent `sin(t)`.

The critical challenge is matching `x*exp(-|x|)`. None of the candidates contain explicit `exp(-|x|)` terms. Let me check what functional forms are available:

- `x*log(c*|x| + 1)` — this is NOT `x*exp(-|x|)`
- `x*|x|` — this equals `x²*sign(x)`, not `x*exp(-|x|)`
- `x*exp(c*x²)` — this is Gaussian-like, not `exp(-|x|)`
- Rational functions like `x/(c + x²)`, `x³/(c + x²)` — these are rational, not exponential decay

The function `x*exp(-|x|)` has very specific behavior: it decays exponentially for large |x|. None of the available building blocks can reproduce this:

- `x*log(c*|x| + 1)` grows (albeit slowly) for large |x|
- `x*|x|` grows quadratically
- Rational functions like `x/(c + x²)` decay as `1/x` for large x, not exponentially
- `x*exp(c*x²)` with c < 0 gives Gaussian decay, not exponential decay

However, let me reconsider. Could combinations of terms approximate or exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)`? For exact equivalence, we need the functional form to match for ALL x values.

No finite combination of polynomials, rational functions, logarithms, and `|x|` terms can equal `x*exp(-|x|)` for all x. These are fundamentally different classes of functions.

For #12: `x*exp(c9*x²)` — setting c9 to a negative value gives Gaussian decay, but `exp(-x²) ≠ exp(-|x|)` for all x. These are different functions.

For #20: The exponential is multiplied by `cos(c9 + t)`, so it would make the t-dependence wrong (mixing x and t in a product).

Let me also verify: is there any algebraic identity that could make rational functions equal to `exp(-|x|)`? No — `exp(-|x|)` is transcendental and cannot be expressed as any finite combination of rational functions, powers, logarithms of polynomials, etc.

The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is an essential component of the GT, and none of the candidate formulas contain building blocks that can reproduce it exactly. The candidates use:
- Polynomial/rational terms in x
- `x*log(c*|x| + 1)` terms
